Warmth in the Heart (372) · Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 17: Skillful in Maintaining Youth, Emerald Eyebrows Blended; No Way to Extend Life, the Golden Market Covets Fine Horses

From then on, Hua Yuanchun stuffed that white gold watch into the corner of the drawer. There was originally a box for it, but now that box had actually become "returning the case while buying the pearl", and was thrown somewhere. One day, while looking for something else, she rummaged through the drawer. She didn't find what she was looking for, but she saw the white gold watch again. She saw that the small diamonds around it were filled with a lot of dust, and the white color was also dim. Hua Yuanchun couldn't help but think of the young man from Nanyang who gave her the watch. He was so generous and extravagant. She wondered when he would come to Shanghai again. She quickly used a small toothbrush to carefully brush away the dust from the diamonds. She also wiped the surface of the white gold. She found another box and put it in, placing it in the jewelry box. After all, that white gold watch had been gathering dust outside all this time, but now it was welcomed back to the palace. Now Hua Lao Liu thought of that white gold watch again, thinking that it was worth five hundred yuan. Even if she discounted it by 80%, she could pawn it for one hundred yuan. If she added some other things, it would be almost enough. So she solemnly took it out of the jewelry box. Because her partner was clumsy, she entrusted A Jinjie in the room to do it. She also told her that this was white gold, which was several times more expensive and better than gold. Don't let the pawnshop think it's silver. This was given to me by a former lover. He spent five or six thousand yuan on me, and only gave me this watch as a souvenir. Once I have money, I will redeem it. A Jinjie happily took the watch to the pawnshop. It was transferred from the hands of the appraiser in the third counter to the appraiser in the second counter, and then from the hands of the appraiser in the second counter to the appraiser in the first counter. The appraiser in the first counter took off his old-fashioned copper-rimmed glasses, looked at it again and again, and then used a small microscope, closed one eye and looked at it for a long time. Then he opened the watch and listened to it next to his ear for a long time before saying that it could be pawned for thirty yuan at most. A Jin said, "This is white gold, several times more expensive and better than gold. Don't be stupid. Look carefully. How can you say that it can only be pawned for thirty yuan? That circle of small diamonds is worth more than thirty yuan." The appraiser in the second counter couldn't tell if the watch was copper, steel, or silver. Now that he heard A Jin say that it was white gold, he carefully looked at the watch again. Because he had never appreciated white gold before. He thought that white gold was nothing special, and it was almost the same as silver. The appraiser in the first counter was already old. He was already furious when he heard A Jin scolding him for being stupid. His beard was standing on end in anger. He sneered and said, "We only know that gold is yellow. We don't know that gold is white. What white gold? We say we don't know. That's what the foreigners use to deceive Chinese children."

American Cotton Gradually Shows Signs of Turning Around

▲ Cotton Cloth Market Conditions Are Quite Good

A New York telegram on the 20th reported on the cotton market situation for the week, stating: "The news from India is encouraging, Lancashire textile factories have also decided to resume work, and domestic demand for cotton cloth has increased. Due to these factors, industry players are buying, and short position holders are covering their positions. Agency firms also have some demand, and brokers are also buying, mostly on behalf of Japanese clients. Demand from Liverpool and Europe is still strong. According to news from Liverpool, Mumbai almost daily purchases raw cotton in Liverpool. When the October contract rises to 1.2 cents, demand gradually decreases, and reactive sentiment arises. The reasons for this are partly that the actual position is easier to loosen, and partly that high prices lead to concerns about excessive cotton planting. However, buy orders during price drops are often absorbed by industry players. Rainfall in the South has delayed cotton harvesting work in several areas, but new cotton crops are reportedly progressing well. According to several sources, since 1925, the planting work at this time of year has never been as extensive as it is this year."

Another report states: "Cotton market sentiment is stable, and European purchases are the highest. The general picture is that of short position holders covering positions and industry players settling prices. Spot demand is still good, and base prices are slightly firm. More textiles are being traded. Recent months have been slightly softer because the reduction in cotton acreage is not as large as expected. Bullish sentiment has eased."

Another report states: "The liquidation of long positions at the end of last year and the slight drop in market prices led to a very unsatisfactory situation in the cotton cloth market. However, conditions gradually improved in January, prices became firmer, and sales were also more extensive, especially for goods that had undergone finishing processes. Sales in the first six weeks of this year reportedly exceeded production by 20%. Cloth prices loosened in early February, while cotton prices rose, causing considerable concern for manufacturers, as sales have recently decreased slightly. However, it was not long before buyers increased, competing to place orders, and cloth prices are now firmer. Although sales are currently good and inventories are low, there is no profit to be made at current prices. Cloth prices have an upward trend, but there are fears that sales will increase. Some factories may abandon their plans to continue reducing production in March. 70% of factories will abolish night work for female and child laborers starting March 1. If another 5% of the cotton industry supports this move, then night work for women and children can be abolished at that time. It is thought that this matter can be achieved. Wheat Futures Rise Step by Step

▲ Market Sentiment is Unusually High

Yesterday, the wheat futures market saw price increases in all contract months in both the morning and afternoon sessions. Recent prices for foreign wheat are no longer as low as they were before the market closure. Generally, short sellers lack the ability to continue trading. The price of foreign wheat, referring only to Australian wheat, must be around six qian. As for Chicago and Canadian wheat, there are no comparative prices. Looking at the distant months, the heavy spring snow may affect future harvests. Compared to previous years, prices are still at reasonable levels. Therefore, market sentiment among both industry insiders and outsiders is uniformly high. Buyers are numerous, while sellers are scarce. It is also heard that speculative long position holders in the yarn and cloth industry are buying without regard to price, causing the market to rise higher and higher. As a result, the current month contract rose by 1 qian and 6 fen compared to before the market closure, the March contract rose by 1 qian and 5 fen, the April and May contracts rose by 1 qian and 4 fen, the June contract rose by 2 qian and 2 fen, and the July contract rose by 2 qian and 3 fen. Because of the market confusion, there are no spot wheat transactions.

Flour Market Rises Enthusiastically

▲ Numerous Outsiders are Continuously Absorbing

Yesterday, the flour market showed a frenzied state in all contract months after the morning opening. After a ten-day closure, the foreign exchange market remained tight, and the price of foreign wheat was shouting higher and higher due to exchange rate factors. Before the closure, Australian wheat had called for 3 taels 9 qian and 5-6 fen. After the closure, it shouted up to about 4 taels and 6 qian. In a blink of an eye, there seemed to be a difference of 6 qian and 5 fen. In addition, the factory's spot flour initially opened at 2 qian and 5 fen, then shouted up to 3 qian. With these factors accumulating, the market's frenzied rise had become impossible to suppress. In addition, outsiders and some Yingkou merchants were absorbing along with the market, making the market even more agitated. At its highest, the near-term contracts reached five or six fen, and the distant-term contracts reached qian Xu. Subsequently, the factory continued and the distant-term contracts fell back by two or three fen. Until the beginning of the afternoon opening, sentiment softened because the gold price reported a decline. Finally, the market turned higher again due to the continuous absorption of outsiders. As a final result, the current month contract rose by 6 fen and 2.5 li compared to before the closure, the March contract rose by 5 fen and 7.5 li, the April and May contracts rose by 6 fen and 7.5 li, the June contract rose by 7 fen and 7.5 li, and the July contract rose by 8 fen and 7.5 li.

Illiterate Citizens

▲ Also Have the Right to Vote in the National Assembly

The Shanghai County Government received an order from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs yesterday, stating: "To issue an order for implementation, according to the Jiangsu Provincial Party Affairs Consolidation Committee's letter, which states: 'Regarding the issue of the right to vote for illiterate representatives in people's organizations, we previously sent personnel to consult with the Central Training Department. The explanation given at that time was that for illiterate representatives, the chairman of the assembly could designate personnel to fill out the ballot on their behalf, based on the representative's opinions. Their right to vote and be elected cannot be deprived simply because they are not good at writing. Given the current situation in our country, more than 80% of the population is illiterate. During this period of political tutelage, implementing civil rights training, the majority of the illiterate population should not be excluded from the scope of training, nor should they be denied the rights they are entitled to within the assembly simply because they are illiterate. Our committee's former Training Department has already instructed the organization instructors of people's organizations in various districts accordingly. We hereby send a letter for your reference and request that you inform your subordinates accordingly.'" In response to this, in addition to forwarding the letter, we hereby order the County Magistrate to inform your subordinates accordingly. This order.

Misinformation Regarding a Large Sum of Stolen Money from the Bank of Communications

▲ Actual Loss: $920

▲ Reimbursed by the Guarantor

Rumors circulated in this city that the Bank of Communications had a large sum of money stolen, with some saying $2.5 million and others claiming even more. For a time, the whole city was in an uproar, regarding it as a major theft. Considering the gravity of the situation, this newspaper investigated from all sides yesterday and learned that the facts were a misunderstanding. It turns out that the bank usually adopts a rotational method for checking banknotes. After person A counts them, they are handed over to person B, and after person B counts them, they are handed over to person C. Since they are checked in rotation, there have never been any mistakes. This time, a certain junior employee privately took $920 in banknotes while counting them and secreted them out. When the counting was finished, there was a shortage of banknotes. The superior bank staff, for the sake of caution, went to the vault to recount them. At that time, the cashier was out on official business due to receiving money, as it was still early for the vault check. When the vault checkers arrived and saw that the cashier was absent, they became very suspicious, thinking that if the cashier was involved in embezzlement, the amount lost would be more than just this small sum. All sorts of misunderstandings thus arose. However, the cashier had been working for many years and was honest and reliable. Just as they were in doubt, the cashier returned, explaining the reason for the absence, and the suspicions were cleared. The junior employee had not returned to the bank for a long time, so the truth became clear, and the guarantor was held accountable. The guarantor then reimbursed the full amount, and the matter was put to rest.

Extension of the Unified Tax Deadline for Cotton Yarn Inventory

▲ The Unified Tax Bureau Telegraphed Branch Chiefs to Extend the Deadline to the End of March

After the implementation of the unified tax on cotton yarn ex-factory from February 1st, for the inventory before February 1st, a pass would be issued after reporting to the Unified Tax Bureau and having personnel verify it, with a deadline of clearing the inventory by the 16th. The Chinese Cotton Mill Association thought that the time was too tight, and in fact, it was impossible to clear the inventory within the deadline. The association then requested the Unified Tax Bureau to extend the deadline. It has been approved by the Ministry of Finance to extend the deadline to the end of March, as reported previously. It is now learned that the Unified Tax Bureau telegraphed the various regional bureaus the day before yesterday to comply with the order. The telegram stated, "The procedures for collecting tax on cotton yarn ex-factory have been discussed and six temporary and simplified methods have been agreed upon with the Chinese Cotton Mill Association and the general representatives of manufacturers in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui, and have been telegraphed to you for compliance on Yu Day. Regarding the matter of exempting the inventory before February 1st from the unified tax and continuing to transport and sell as before, the original deadline was February 16th for clearing all inventory, and taxes would be collected according to regulations after the deadline. Now, the association has petitioned for an extension, and the Ministry has issued an order stating that the first half of February coincided with the Lunar New Year holiday, and transportation was suspended, which is somewhat difficult in commercial customs, and it is considered realistic after reviewing. The transport and sale of inventory is tentatively allowed to be extended until March 31st, and there will be no further extensions after this. This should be complied with. In addition to replying to the Yarn Merchants Association in writing and sending separate telegrams, it is hereby telegraphed for compliance. Director Xie Huixing."

A Comparison of the Advantages and Disadvantages for Chinese and Japanese Yarn Merchants After the Implementation of the Unified Cotton Yarn Tax

▲ Chinese Merchants are Being Over-Taxed

The Guowen News Agency reports that the cotton yarn tax was originally collected by the customs in four grades. This time, it has been changed to a unified tax, and the Ministry of Finance originally intended to divide it into three grades, but later, following the demands of the Japanese merchants, it was decided to have two tax rates, namely 2.75 yuan per dan for 23 counts and below, and 3.75 yuan per dan for 23 counts and above. In reality, most of the Chinese yarn is 23 counts and below, while most of the Japanese yarn is 23 counts and above. For example, for Japanese 40 count yarn, valued at 300 taels, the tax is 3.75 yuan. For Chinese 14 count yarn, valued at 150 taels, the tax is 2.75 yuan. This means that for yarn with a difference in value of half, on average, Chinese merchants should only pay 1.875 yuan in unified tax, but they are being over-taxed by 0.875 yuan. The Chinese yarn mills association believes that this tax rate is obviously unfair and has submitted a report to the authorities, requesting a revised and fair tax rate. The following is a translation of the Japanese perspective as reported in the Shanghai Mainichi Shimbun for clarification: (The following is a partial translation of the Shanghai Mainichi Shimbun) After the implementation of the unified cotton yarn tax, there is no difference between Chinese and foreign yarn mills. It is uniformly stipulated that 2.75 yuan per 100 catties will be charged for 23 counts and below, and 3.75 yuan per 100 catties will be charged for 23 counts and above. After the implementation of this unified tax, what are the advantages and disadvantages for the Chinese and Japanese yarn mills that are in opposition? This is worthy of general attention. The implementation of the unified tax will bring the most favorable conditions to Japanese yarn mills. The initial report said that the unit system would not be used for taxation, and the same type of tax would also be levied on imported cotton yarn, so the threat of foreign cotton yarn can be completely eliminated. In addition, the recent sharp decline in silver prices means there is no hope of recovery for a time, so taxing in gold units at customs is tantamount to increasing tariffs. Imposing a new tariff in gold units on imported goods and a unified tax in silver units on domestic products is the most effective condition for resisting foreign products. Although Sino-Japanese yarn mills in China have the same favorable conditions, the superior position of Japanese merchants over Chinese merchants lies in the division of tax rates, which is the so-called 23 counts as the boundary. The Ministry of Finance’s initial proposal was to have three types, but the Japanese merchants advocated two types, and the result was two tax rates. Chinese and Japanese yarn mills originally had a boundary between coarse and fine yarn. Japanese mills focus on 20 counts and 42 counts, while Chinese mills focus on 20 counts and 16 counts. Now, it is stipulated that 2.75 yuan per 100 catties will be charged for 23 counts and below, so yarn that is close to 23 counts is the most beneficial, which is very clear. Chinese merchants focusing on 10 counts and 16 counts will be at a disadvantage compared to Japanese merchants focusing on 20 counts. As for 23 counts and above, 3.75 yuan per 100 catties will be charged, so there is no disadvantage for Japanese merchants focusing on 42 counts. Moreover, in the future, the upgrading of products will be even more effective in resisting imported goods. Last year, the implementation of the ex-factory tax on tobacco caused Chinese cigarette companies to fall into poverty and be monopolized by British and American tobacco companies. Therefore, the implementation of the unified cotton yarn tax today will not be a loss for Japanese yarn mills. Instead, it can gradually solve the previous problems.

The Silk and Satin Industry Requests a Temporary Exemption from the Special Tax on Textiles

▲ And Presents Future Standards for Taxation

The Shanghai Silk and Satin Trade Association submitted a joint report to the Ministries of Industry and Finance yesterday, requesting a temporary exemption from the special tax on textiles. The original report stated: "Concerning the item of textile tax stipulated in the Special Tax Regulations, the tax rate is still under review. We hereby present the current situation of the silk and satin industry, list the future standards for taxation, and request a temporary exemption for several years to allow for recovery, in the hope that you will review, approve, and implement it. It is noted that the special consumption tax regulations promulgated by the Ministry of Finance on December 18th of the 17th year of the Republic of China, Article 2 stipulates that the items subject to special consumption tax include sugar and textiles, etc. Article 4 states that silk tax will be refunded when silk products are taxed. Since the implementation of the 'licentiation fee' system, the taxes that the silk and satin industry should bear are (1) the business tax that each province and city plans to implement, and (2) the special tax that the central government plans to implement in the future. According to the aforementioned regulations, there is no doubt that at a time when the silk and satin business is declining, the implementation of new taxes will inevitably increase the burden and hinder the development of the silkworm industry. Although the special tax regulations are still under review by the ministries, we dare not speculate. However, the Hangzhou Silk Industry Association, because this matter is related to the sideline business of farmers, the livelihood of machine workers, and the business of manufacturers, should be addressed first, and a report was submitted to the ministries, requesting exemption from the special tax within a certain number of years. Considering the situation, it is because the silk weaving factories in Hangzhou have suffered deeply from the impact in recent years that they have made this urgent appeal. The silk industry groups in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have also jointly elected representatives to petition for a temporary tax exemption for three years. The industry's suffering has been detailed in this report, and it is hoped that it will be clearly understood. This association would like to add to the suggestions made by the Hangzhou Silk Industry Association and present them to the ministries. It is noted that since the textile tax is stipulated as one of the special taxes, the association's request for tax exemption may be considered an exception to the regulations, as there is no explicit provision in the regulations. However, the original report has a limitation of a certain number of years, which is different from directly requesting tax exemption. Moreover, according to the precedents of recent years, sugar and iron are both taxable items. However, companies such as National Sugar Manufacturing Company, Puyi Sugar Manufacturing Company, Yangzi Iron Manufacturing Company in Hankou, and Hexing Steel Factory in Shanghai have all been granted special tax exemptions for a certain number of years. These are all exceptions, and sugar is a food necessity, while silk and satin are clothing necessities, and the situations are similar. Moreover, special tax exemptions and the issuance of public bonds are both national policies to rescue industries. However, the silk factory industry issued public bonds this time to rescue the industry after all the silk factories had been shut down, which cost a lot of effort and caused great losses. It is better to take advantage of the fact that the silk weaving industry has not yet been completely ruined and temporarily exempt it from special taxes for several years to allow it to recover slightly and gradually restore industrial and commercial vitality. Indirectly protecting the reality is much more valuable than waiting for the collapse of the silk factory industry and then rushing to rescue it. The gains and losses are far apart. Moreover, comparing the silk and satin industries, although factory silk has Japan as its strong competitor, encroaching on sales channels, it is still necessary for foreign silk factories as raw materials, so various countries tax it lightly, and it is still a major foreign trade to this day. Silk and satin, on the other hand, are finished products rather than raw materials, so they are first subjected to the harsh

Page 14

tax of Korea and then to the heavy tax of Vietnam, and foreign sales channels are almost completely deprived. Although silk and satin are in the same difficult environment, in reality, the silk and satin industry is more urgent than factory silk. This time, the association's request for tax exemption for several years is feared that outsiders may not fully understand their suffering and turn to suspect their intentions of extravagance. This is because they are used to the wrong things being right, and the relationship is extremely important. Therefore, we dare to forget the trouble and hope that the following situation can reach the ears of Qing Dynasty officials. Secondly, the original report of the association has a request for a temporary tax exemption for several years. That is, tax exemption is originally temporary, and the tax rate should be determined first, so that when the tax exemption period expires, the government can follow its own procedures, and the silk and satin industry will not be at a loss due to drastic changes. Article 3 of the Special Consumption Tax Regulations stipulates that the consumption tax rate is divided into three types: daily necessities, semi-luxury goods, and luxury goods, and each is taxed at a corresponding rate. This time, the provinces and cities are implementing business tax and have failed to examine the history and national conditions, and many have mistakenly regarded silk and satin as luxury goods. Since the Ministry of Industry declared that silk and satin are special domestic products of our country and need to be protected, and that their use is also for the daily necessities of the common people, the Executive Yuan issued an order to the ministries and provinces to comply. It has been concluded, and it should be requested to handle the taxation according to the tax standard of daily necessities when stipulating the special tax rate in the future. This will be in line with the Yuan Order and will take into account the commercial situation. It is proposed to apply the daily necessities tax to the special tax on silk and satin, and to temporarily exempt the tax for several years as stated by the Hangzhou Association, so as to allow for relief. It is for the public good to submit all the reasons to the Yuan Department for review and approval. "Sincerely, the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry.

The Hotel Industry Requests Revision of the Business Tax

▲ Lists Five Points

The Shanghai Hotel Industry Association stated that the business tax rate for the industry is 20 per mille, which is too heavy to bear. Yesterday, they submitted a report to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, requesting them to forward it to the Ministry of Finance and the Municipal Government for revision and reduction. The original report was very long. The summary is as follows: "We are submitting a report to request forwarding. Recently, we read the Jiangsu Provincial Government's regulations on the collection of business tax and the tax rate table, which exceeds the standards issued by the Ministry by eight or nine times. Our industry belongs to the hotel industry, and the hotel industry has always been misunderstood by outsiders as a seemingly prosperous business. However, the provincial government did not carefully examine the situation and hastily set the tax rate for our industry at 20 per mille, ranking it alongside game halls and luxury goods. This seems to be inconsistent with the Ministry's original guidelines. Upon hearing this, all hotels were alarmed and requested a reduction. Our association originally intended to speak out and apply earlier, but we considered that paying taxes to the party-led government is the duty of revolutionary citizens. Therefore, we had to carefully consider the situation from the perspectives of both the higher and lower levels, and act cautiously between ourselves and others. Although we have made every effort to explain, we are unable to bear this excessive burden in fact, and it will also lose its balance in terms of civil rights. Therefore, we must state the reasons for the request for reduction as follows: (1) It is a mistake to regard 'sightseeing' as a standard for business taxation; (2) It is a mistake to rank hotels alongside luxury goods as a standard for taxation; (3) It is a mistake to rank hotels alongside cosmetics and game halls as a standard for taxation; (4) It is a mistake to use the 'licentiation fee' system as a compensation for tax collection; (5) The appropriate and fair tax amount that the hotel industry should pay. The above five points can generally illustrate the difficulties faced by the hotel industry and the fact that it is impossible to levy an excessive amount of tax. The rationale of barely accepting 2 per mille is extremely obvious and can be determined. There are other points that have not yet been mentioned. In this city, there are no losses from the 'licentiation fee' system, and the business tax can be implemented later to allow the people of this city to recover slightly. If it is necessary to implement it, it should be applied equally to both Chinese and foreign businesses. Otherwise, foreign goods will be easier to sell, and domestic products will be hindered from being promoted. As for the hotels with the highest profits, they are the hotels established by foreigners, such as Hua Mao, Li Cha, Da Hua, and other stores. They also lead the way in luxury consumption. The hotels established by Chinese people are not only unable to reach their level, but also only eat their leftovers. Moreover, with the daily decline of the Chinese economy, how many people can afford to stay in hotels and spend money? If Chinese merchants are taxed but foreign merchants are not, the selling price will not be much different, and the Western hotels will be equal or even cheaper, which will inevitably attract Chinese customers to flock to them. The Chinese hotels will suffer a blow, which is not the way for the state to protect businesses responsibly. Our association is concerned about safety and cannot avoid being verbose in order to seek correction from those who know the situation, and we earnestly request your association to forward our request to the Ministry of Finance and the Municipal Government for prompt review and approval, and to levy taxes according to the 2 per mille standard set by the Ministry, so as to alleviate the difficulties of businessmen in the hotel industry and allow hundreds and thousands of hotel businessmen and workers to retain a share of their livelihood. We will be grateful for this." Sincerely, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

The Executive Yuan Orders Business Tax on the Silk and Satin Industry to be Collected as Daily Necessities

▲ Stipulates That It Must Not Exceed 2 per Mille

▲ Has Been Separately Ordered to Provincial and Municipal Governments for Compliance

The Silk and Satin Trade Association stated that the business tax rates stipulated by the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces for the silk and satin industry were too high to bear, and that silk and satin were daily necessities for the common people, but they were regarded as luxury businesses, which was not in line with the intention of maintaining people's livelihood and promoting domestic products. After convening a joint meeting of representatives from the Hangzhou Silk and Satin Trade Association, it was resolved to base the decision on Article 4 of the guidelines issued by the Ministry, which stipulates that the standard should not exceed 2 per mille. More than a dozen people, including Luo Qinghua, Wang Yansong, Lu Zhengbing, Lin Zhaoren, Cai Liangyou, and Zhu Mouguang, were sent as representatives to go to Beijing with a petition to request a reduction. The ministers of the various Yuan departments of the National Government agreed to adopt their recommendations as much as possible, and the Ministry of Industry submitted its opinions and forwarded them to the Executive Yuan for instructions. The following is the telegram from the Ministry of Industry: "To the Shanghai Silk and Satin Trade Association, It has been found that in the case of the previous request to review and reduce the business tax on silk fabrics in Zhejiang Province, we have added our opinions and submitted them to the Executive Yuan for review and instructions, and have telegraphed the Zhejiang Provincial Government for review and handling. We have now received an order from the Executive Yuan stating: "We have received the report stating that silk and satin are special domestic products and need to be protected, and their use is also for the daily necessities of the common people. Please order all provinces to collect this business tax, and the tax rate shall not exceed 2 per mille to maintain it. This is in line with the previous instructions from the Central Government to rescue the silk weaving industry and should be approved. Please wait for an order to be issued to the Ministry of Finance and the provincial and municipal governments to comply with this order." The Ministry of Industry is hereby informed. (Stamp of the Ministry of Industry)"

The Fujian Navy Aircraft Manufacturing Plant Has Moved to Shanghai

▲ More Than 130 Employees Arrived Yesterday

The Navy's Majiang Aircraft Manufacturing Plant was ordered to move to Shanghai and be placed under the jurisdiction of the Jiangnan Shipyard in this city. At 1 AM the night before last, all the personnel and machinery of the plant were transported to Shanghai on the Navy's Jing'an transport ship. They stayed overnight at the Songkou docks and entered the port in the early morning yesterday, disembarking at the Gaochangmiao Naval Pier. A reporter from the Guowen News Agency visited in the afternoon and met with the Deputy Director of the plant, Mr. Zeng Yijing. The details are recorded below:

▲ Personnel Arriving in Shanghai: Yesterday, there were 12 staff members and more than 120 craftsmen. The Director, Wang Zhu, was ill in Fujian and did not come. The staff members who arrived yesterday included Deputy Director Zeng Yijing, accountants Zheng Baoyuan, Chen Gengyao, Huang Weibiong, Lin Kengran, Chen Liyi, engineers Wang Chonghong and Wang Zongzhu, material managers Shi Shengde and Ding Ting, and engineering auditors Li Chen and Liu Jijiang, etc.

▲ What Mr. Zeng Said: Deputy Director Zeng Yijing told the reporter, "Our plant in Fujian was subordinate to the Majiang Shipbuilding Bureau, which was founded during the Tongzhi period of the Qing Dynasty by Zeng Guofan and was the birthplace of the Chinese Navy. Our plant was established in the eighth year of the Republic of China, when Director Wang Zhu and the four of us had just returned from overseas. Seeing the effectiveness of aviation and hoping to develop it, we established an aviation plant and a manufacturing plant. It has been more than ten years since then, so the staff of our plant are still the first graduates, and the craftsmen were also recruited from ten years ago. During this period, we have manufactured more than a dozen seaplanes, including the Jiang Wei, Jiang Fu, Jiang Ying, and Hai Diao. Due to financial constraints, we have not been able to manufacture actively. With today's hundred or so employees, if we have sufficient funds again, we can manufacture one plane every two months, six planes a year, which is easy. The monthly recurring expenses of our plant in Fujian were 5,000 yuan, but the living expenses in Shanghai and Fujian are very different, so we plan to ask the Ministry to increase it. All the manufacturing machinery was brought to Shanghai yesterday. Fortunately, the shipyard has everything, and if there is any shortage in the future, we can borrow it. The five seaplanes Hai Diao, Hai Peng, Jiang Lu, Jiang Fu, and Jiang Ying have been handed over to the Naval Aviation Plant in Fujian for use, and we did not bring them to Shanghai this time."

The Anti-Opium Society's Reply to Wu Liande's Letter

On the 17th of this month, Mr. Wu Liande sent a letter to the Chinese National Anti-Opium Society. The society specially prepared a letter to reply as follows: "Dear Sir, We received your letter on the 14th. Here is a separate reply: (1) After you published an article in various newspapers entitled "The Extremely Toxic Problem of Opium Pills," fair criticisms were published in the Da Wan Bao on February 10th, the Shanghai Shishi Xinbao on February 12th, the Central Daily News on February 14th, the Shanghai Minguo Daily on February 16th, the Millard's Review on February 14th and 19th, and the public opinion circles in North China. Chinese and foreign public opinion unanimously recognizes this claim as a state monopoly, and this association, in order to implement its consistent claims, cannot remain silent. Your letter actually said that "Liande is praised for advocating the state monopoly of opium." Public opinion is like this, there is no need to argue. (2) This association adheres to the late Premier's instructions on anti-opium and represents the public opinion of the people to promote the anti-opium movement. All claims are for the entire action. This protest against the state monopoly of opium is not an individual claim, but the public opinion of the entire association. Your letter involves the association's Secretary-General Huang, which is a misunderstanding. This is hereby stated. (3) You were listed as an Executive Committee member at the fifth annual meeting of this association on December 26th, 1918 of the Republic of China, which was produced legally by election. There is no reason to seek consent in advance. Moreover, you have repeatedly attended meetings, such as on September 30th and December 2nd, 1919, and you personally attended the meetings. How can there be such a thing as "listing a humble name without obtaining prior consent" as mentioned in the letter? This matter concerns the credibility of both parties and should be based on facts to avoid mishearing. In addition to submitting your letter to the Executive Committee, we should reply to you first.

The Second Branch of the High Court Releases a Political Prisoner

▲ Fu Yuqin Has Been Approved for Release

▲ The Remaining Prisoners Are Under Review by the High Court

In the case of the National Government's amnesty for political prisoners on New Year's Day in the 20th year of the Republic of China, it was stipulated that the higher courts of each province should organize a review committee to handle the amnesty in accordance with the amnesty regulations. The political prisoners in Shanghai were sent by the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court to the Suzhou Higher Court for handling. It is said that the political prisoner cases sent from Shanghai totaled more than 100 cases, involving more than 200 political prisoners, most of whom were young students, and most of the cases were anti-revolutionary and communist. The High Court branch sent the cases several weeks ago, and the Suzhou High Court has not yet completed the review due to careful review and research. It is now learned that only one person has been approved for release because he meets the amnesty regulations. This person is a student named Fu Yuqin from Danxian County, Guangdong Province. He is 23 years old this year. On October 13th of the 19th year, at 12 noon, he carried 18 packages of a book called "Xin Qiongyai" totaling 36 copies, intending to go to the post office to send them to various ports in Tianjin for propaganda. He was arrested by Western patrolman Shaa'er Sipei and Japanese patrolman Shaolin Jiuji on Robert Sun Road in western Shanghai and sent to the court for trial. On November 7th, he was sentenced to six months in prison. The High Court branch received a reply from the Suzhou High Court a few days ago and immediately released him from prison. The remaining prisoners will have to wait until the review and approval are completed before they can be released.

China Industrial and Commercial Management Association Holds Second Luncheon Discussion Meeting

▲Chairman Kong Made a Special Trip to Shanghai Yesterday to Attend

▲Speeches by Doctors Dai Leren and Guo Bingwen

The China Industrial and Commercial Management Association held its second luncheon meeting yesterday at the Bankers Club. The association's chairman, Dr. Kong Yongzhi, in accordance with the previous resolution to emulate the Rotary International model, holds a luncheon discussion meeting every two weeks, and insisted on holding the meeting on schedule. Therefore, he made a special trip from Nanjing to Shanghai yesterday to preside over the meeting. Attendees included Liu Hongsheng, Yenching University Professor Dr. Dai Leren, Xu Ji, Zhao Jinqing, Shou Yicheng, Pan Xulun, Qian Chengxu, Zou Bingwen, Yao Yongli, Xu Zhiyi, Zhang Zilian, Guo Bingwen, Chen Liting, Hua Runquan, Tao Leqin, Xu Dinglan, Zhong Ketuo, Chen Fuqing, Zhang Xianglin, Qi Fuming, Li Weimin, Zhu Longxiang, Zhou Zhongqian, Xu Xie Kang, He Dekui, along with Secretary-General Cao Yunxiang and staff members of the secretariat. The meeting was chaired by Chairman Kong. First, Secretary-General Cao Yunxiang led the singing of the China Industrial and Commercial Management Association's anthem, which was adapted from the Yale University football song and was quite interesting. Next, Professor Dai Leren, Director of the Livelihood Improvement Research Association, was invited to speak about the origins of the Livelihood Improvement Research Association and its willingness to cooperate with the association. He also mentioned that the association had invited Professor R. H. Tawney of the University of London to come to China to lecture. Tawney is extremely knowledgeable in industrial and commercial management issues and is currently in China investigating factory conditions. He would welcome members of the association to discuss practical issues with him. Tomorrow (the 22nd), he will give a speech at the YMCA on Sichuan Road on "Factors in the Progress of the British Labor Movement," and he hoped that members of the association would attend. Next, Dr. Guo Bingwen was invited to speak about the British National Industrial and Commercial Discussion Conference, and the organization and work of the Taylor Society of Scientific Management, which could provide many references for China. He also said that scientific management is practical and not just a name. Chinese schools also have specialized departments in factory management, but the theory and practice are not adapted to each other, which is a pity. The association is correcting this shortcoming, and its future success can be assured. Subsequently, Zhong Ketuo, He Dekui, Cao Yunxiang, Zou Bingwen, and others expressed their opinions on developing the affairs of the Industrial and Commercial Management Association. Finally, Chairman Kong gave a speech, briefly stating that the National Government had approved an annual subsidy of 9,600 yuan for the association. He hoped that the association would actively carry out practical research on industrial improvement issues. He also mentioned that 8 million yuan of Jiangsu-Zhejiang silk industry bonds were planned to be used to improve silk industry research and other matters, so that silk factories could gradually implement scientific management methods, and he hoped that other industries would follow suit and strive for improvement, so that a new life for China's industrial sector would be possible. The guests and hosts enjoyed themselves, and the meeting ended at around 2:00 PM.

The association believes that there are many issues that should be discussed during the implementation of the Factory Law, so it is scheduled to hold a discussion meeting on the implementation of the Factory Law at the United General Assembly next Saturday at noon. The third luncheon discussion meeting is scheduled to be held on March 7th. It is also heard that Huang Boqiao, President of the Chinese Institute of Engineers, has been invited to speak on "The Self-Help, Mutual Aid, and National Salvation of China's Industrial, Financial, and Engineering Sectors." It is expected that there will be a grand occasion at that time.

Xunwu County Party Headquarters Requests Troops to Suppress Communists

Xie Pengsheng, the Fifth Company Commander of the 26th Regiment of the Fifth Division, forwarded a telegraphic message from the Xunwu County Party Headquarters of Jiangxi Province to this newspaper yesterday, addressed to the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Jiangxi Provincial Party Headquarters, the Provincial Government, all division, brigade, and regimental commanders suppressing bandits in Jiangxi, and all newspapers: "Heaven has afflicted Xunwu, and years of chaos have resulted in massacres unprecedented in history. Since the March 25th uprising in the 17th year of the Republic, the death toll has reached over 10,000 to date. No less than four thousand houses have been burned, and the loss of public and private property is estimated at over five million yuan. Corpses fill the valleys, a catastrophe of unparalleled scale. Abdomen ripping and heart digging are inhumane. The bandits' ideology originates from hatred, so they kill anyone they encounter during each uprising. Local tyrants are killed, good people are killed, enemies are killed, and even women and children are killed. Those with confused minds who surrender to the bandits are killed after a short time. Wealthy gentry who join opportunistically are also killed. Initially, a small number are killed, then batches are killed. If the main army does not arrive within a day, the killing will not stop for a day. Recently, 3,000 remnants of Zhu Mao's forces have fled from Nankang and Xinfeng, joining the internal bandits and killing each other. The murderous atmosphere is heavy and the sky is dark. In recent days, they have captured Niudouguang, Chetou, Maoping, and other places, causing great pain and adding to the catastrophe. The people of Xunwu are directly suffering, and the national lifeline is indirectly injured. Although the county police force, together with a company of the Pinglian Defense Army, engaged in a desperate close-quarters battle, and the bandits' momentum was somewhat thwarted after a day of fierce fighting, they are exhausted and out of ammunition. In addition, the disparity in numbers is too great, and the result will ultimately be a defeat. The isolated city is in extreme danger, and the lives of the people are truly pitiful, groaning and waiting for death, unable to last another day. Xunwu is also a part of the country, and the people of Xunwu are also citizens. Rescuing the dying and helping the distressed is our duty. However, the superiors believe that Xunwu is far from the province and beyond their reach, so they have implicitly abandoned it. Reading the newspaper, the Central Government has increased the number of divisions led by Sun, Han, and Xu to four to suppress the bandits in Jiangxi. Therefore, we express our difficulties and dangers and plead with all our hearts, earnestly requesting the prompt dispatch of appropriate troops to pursue and suppress the bandits in the county and eradicate them from the root, in order to save the tens of thousands of dying people. Sending troops one day earlier means one more day of life. Adding one soldier means one more point of strength. Otherwise, the devastation will spread, and the people of Xunwu will have no survivors. We are telegraphing while weeping, not knowing what to say. The Xunwu County Party Headquarters of the Chinese Nationalist Party and the people of the entire county kowtow."

Central Bank Inspection Report

▲Eighty-First Time

The eighty-first inspection report on the issuance reserves of the Central Bank states: "In accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this committee is responsible for inspecting the reserve funds for the issuance of convertible banknotes by the bank. The eighty-first inspection was conducted at the bank's Issuance Bureau on February 20, 1941, and the results of the inspection are announced as follows: The total amount of convertible banknotes issued is 26,291,912 silver dollars, including 25,424,412 silver dollar notes and 867,500 yuan in subsidiary currency notes. The total amount of convertible banknote reserves is 26,291,912 silver dollars, including 22,840,472 silver dollars in cash reserves. These cash reserves include 17,227,837.27 yuan stored in the bank's issuance vault, 2,133,117 yuan stored in branches in various ports, and 3,479,517.73 yuan deposited with fellow banks. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 3,451,440 silver dollars. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Banknote Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guarantee reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash exceeds 60% and the guarantee is less than 40%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This is a special report. February 20, 1941. Li Fusun, Chairman of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank; Supervisors Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou.

Xu Ji."

Trial Opens in the Fuchang Lawsuit, One of Huang Chujiu's Businesses

▲Company Assets Already Mortgaged

▲Plaintiff Asks for Judgment Before Further Discussion

▲Debate Concludes, Judgment Scheduled

Huang Chujiu operated many types of businesses during his lifetime, and after his death, the Riyue Bank and the Dashijie Amusement Savings were the first to cease operations. Depositors made various claims to protect their rights. In addition to these two businesses, the Fuchang Tobacco Company has also been preemptively seized by the creditor in accordance with the Special District Local Court.

Fuchang was closed because the raw materials for Fuchang Company's manufacturing were supplied by Meihua, Youyi, Meifeng, Lianmei, and other four tobacco leaf companies. It owed Meihua more than 98,800 taels of silver in goods, owed Youyi more than 29,700 taels, owed Meifeng 20,000 taels, and owed Lianmei more than 17,500 taels. There were instances where promissory notes were issued to various creditors, but the payments were not made when due. The creditors filed a lawsuit with the Special Court, requesting a judgment ordering Huang Chujiu's two sons, Xianzhong and Xinyao, and Fuchang manager Yao Jixian, to jointly repay the debts. Fearing that the defendants would hide Fuchang's assets, they requested that the company be sealed first. Since the company has been sealed, tobacco production has also been suspended.

▲Assets Already Mortgaged However, after the seal was issued, the American firm Huizhong suddenly had a lawyer submit a petition to the Special Court, stating that all of the company's assets had been mortgaged to Huizhong, and that other creditors could not interfere. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Wenrong opened the trial and summoned the plaintiffs Meihua and others, who were represented by lawyer Xu Shihao, while the defendants Huang Xianzhong and Xinyao retained lawyer Tan Yigong, and Yao Jixian retained lawyer Wu Zhiping to defend them. Huizhong and the New World Hotel also each retained lawyers to attend the hearing, one for the mortgage and one to pursue rent arrears. Judge Xu instructed the lawyer of Huizhong that mortgage disputes could not be mixed with this case, and that if there were claims, a separate lawsuit for execution objection should be filed. He also instructed the lawyer of the New World Hotel that the rent arrears being pursued should also be filed in a separate case and should not be confused with this one. Both lawyers complied.

▲The Defendants' Defense The interrogation began immediately. The representatives of the plaintiffs Meihua and others stated the amounts owed, and the managers of each plaintiff presented the amounts owed by the defendants, some for the price of goods and some for promissory notes, and submitted the notes to prove the amount of the debt. Lawyer Tan then defended his clients, saying that Huang Xianzhong and Xinyao were initially unaware of the amount Fuchang owed, and that the amounts claimed by the plaintiffs in this case were generally correct, but that Fuchang Company was one of five businesses jointly operated by Gongfa Company, and although Huang Chujiu was the general manager of Fuchang, the actual principal was Gongfa Company. Therefore, Fuchang's shareholders are also Gongfa's shareholders. The general manager is only responsible for liquidation. Now that Huang Chujiu is dead, the responsibility for liquidation has naturally ceased. However, Gongfa Company's assets are currently being liquidated, and it is not yet possible to discuss what responsibilities the shareholders should bear. However, the reasons given by the plaintiffs for requesting the preemptive seizure of Fuchang's assets are somewhat false, as there is no possibility of hiding or moving the seized assets. Now that they have been sealed, the defendants have been affected by the business, and the creditors have no benefit to speak of.

▲Proposed Solutions Judge Xu, after listening to the lawyer's statement, instructed that if there were objections to the preemptive seizure, an appeal could be filed in accordance with the law, and the lawyer did not elaborate further. Wu Zhiping, Yao Jixian's lawyer, then stood up and stated that Yao Jixian was originally Fuchang's assistant manager, and Huang Chujiu was the manager. As for the amounts claimed by the plaintiffs, they were correct, but Fuchang was a part of Gongfa. Fuchang was not registered, and Gongfa was not registered either. The tobacco leaves required for Fuchang's tobacco production were supplied by the plaintiffs. At the end of the previous year, the plaintiffs stopped supplying raw materials, so they had to stop work. An investigation revealed that Fuchang's assets were worth approximately 300,000 yuan, and the amount owed was also 300,000 yuan. The three affiliated movie theaters were worth approximately 100,000 yuan in total. In addition, the share capital was approximately 50,000 to 60,000 yuan. On the debt side, it owed Riyue Bank 800,000 yuan, owed various households approximately 400,000 yuan for goods, and owed Huizhong 100,000 yuan in mortgage money. The two do not match by 400,000 to 500,000 yuan. These are all the losses over the years. Huang Chujiu held the majority of Gongfa shares, so Fuchang was also his major shareholder. Now there are several solutions being considered to discuss with the creditors in order to minimize the losses. The first solution is for the plaintiffs to continue supplying raw materials so that they can continue to manufacture and sell tobacco and gradually repay the debts. The second solution is to sell all the factory buildings and assets, which would be more profitable than an auction. The third solution is to lease them. The fourth solution is to manufacture tobacco for other companies. However, the plaintiffs do not allow the first solution, and the second solution cannot be found in a hurry. Now, they can only request the court to allow the cross-adhesive strips in the machine room to be changed to straight-line adhesive strips, so that workers can still enter and exit the machine room to manufacture cigarettes. The creditors may send people to supervise, so that Fuchang can resume operations, which would also benefit the creditors.

▲Request for Postponement of Judgment Xu Shihao, the lawyer for each plaintiff, then said that the Huizhong Company had published a notice stating that Fuchang

's assets and factory buildings had been sold to Huizhong, but today Fuchang's lawyer said that there was only a mortgage. Outsiders cannot understand the inside story. If the preemptive seizure is lifted, it is difficult to guarantee that there will be no accidents. (Huizhong's lawyer then submitted the contract, but it was in a foreign language, and it was said that it was not a sales contract, but a mortgage.) Now that the facts are clear and the amount claimed has been acknowledged by the other party, the plaintiff's request should be approved and a judgment should be made in accordance with the law. If the defendant wants to seek reconciliation and has a good plan, they can still propose a solution and proceed with reconciliation after the judgment. Lawyer Wu Zhiping still requested a postponement of the judgment, saying that the judgment would make reconciliation difficult.

▲Responsibility The lawyer Tan Yigong then debated the responsibility of Huang Xianzhong and Xinyao in this case, saying that since Fuchang was an affiliated product of Gongfa Company, the plaintiff should first make claims against Gongfa Company's assets. If Gongfa Company's assets are not enough to repay the debts in this case, then they can seek repayment from the shareholders. However, the shareholders are not only Huang Chujiu, and it is still a question whether this debt was incurred before May 19, 1920, or after. Therefore, Huang Xianzhong and Xinyao are not responsible for repayment and should be dismissed.

▲Judgment on the 28th Lawyer Xu Shihao then rebutted, saying that the internal organization of Fuchang was not well known to the plaintiffs, but the goods sent by the plaintiffs were all stamped with Fuchang's Jiu Xing. Jiu Xing and Fuchang are both Huang Chujiu's businesses, so there is no problem. However, since Fuchang is not registered and is not a legal entity, Huang Chujiu should naturally bear full responsibility. The two defendants are Huang's sons and cannot be exempted. The amounts owed were all after May 19, 1920, so there is no question of responsibility. Lawyer Tan then replied that the notice published by Huang's son referred to Huang Chujiu's personal debts, and Huang's son has not yet expressed his intention to inherit the estate and has already expressed his willingness to hand over all of his father's private property. Since Fuchang is a partnership, Huang cannot be solely responsible. After the debate, Judge Xu adjourned the hearing until the morning of the 28th of this month for judgment.

Two Long-Distance Bus Companies Increase Prices

The Shanghai-Minhang-Nanzhe Long-Distance Bus Transportation Company and the Baoshan-Chengsong-Yang Long-Distance Bus Company have submitted reports to the Public Works Bureau, requesting approval to increase fares appropriately in order to compensate for the substantial impact of the recent soaring gold prices on the company's expenses. The bureau has forwarded the report to the municipal government for approval. Chengsong-Yang Company: Chengsong ticket, original price 1.6 cents, new price 1.8 cents; Yangsong ticket, original price 2 cents, new price 2.2 cents; Sanguantang to Chengsong ticket, original price 1 cent, new price 1.1 cents; Sanguantang to Yanghang ticket, original price 1.5 cents, new price 1.6 cents.

Wusong Telephone Temporarily Unable to Recover

Due to the continuous rain and snow in recent days, many telephone poles in Wusong Town have been knocked down and telephone wires have been broken, causing the telephone communication to be completely cut off. It has been a week now. Because the Wusong Telephone Bureau has suffered heavy losses this time, it is temporarily unable to recover. Yesterday, the bureau specially sent an engineer to survey the total loss, which amounted to five or six thousand yuan. However, the bureau's telephone service in the entire town and Baoshan has less than 200 subscribers, with low monthly fees and poor business, and has been in deficit for many years. However, because telephone communication is important, it is still trying its best to maintain the status quo. After suffering this major loss, it is difficult to continue to support it. Therefore, after the bureau's engineer surveyed the loss yesterday, the bureau plans to convene a general meeting of shareholders to discuss solutions. The restoration of telephone communication in the entire town may still take some time.

Chen, the director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, issued instruction document No. 350 from the Water Patrol Team yesterday, stating: "Regarding compliance matters, it is noted that the municipal government issued instruction document No. 7376, stating: 'It is noted that the rowing boat households Shen Xingquan and others have been rowing boats without licenses in the Huangpu River. However, the registration of rowing boats has been closed and licenses cannot be reissued. It is difficult to handle. However, the area of these rowing boats is not much different from that of first-class cargo ships, and the styles are similar. It is proposed that these rowing boats be treated as first-class cargo ships, and a fine of three yuan be imposed in accordance with Article 3 of the cargo ship penalty rules, and they be registered and licensed as first-class cargo ships and pay monthly donations, so as to be slightly flexible in the crackdown.' Therefore, in addition to instructing approval to handle the matter in accordance with the above, the bureau is hereby ordered to promptly instruct compliance and implementation without delay. This order, etc.' After receiving the order, the Xu General Team immediately issued a notice, informing all rowboat households who have not registered and have been detained to come to the team to register in accordance with the regulations and pay the fine, and not to wait and see and mislead themselves."

Runaway Adopted Daughter Returns After Two Months

▲ Has been married and cohabitating for quite some time

Xiong Baishu, a Jiangxi native residing at 757 Avenue Edward VII, who works in the printing industry, had an adopted daughter named Xiong Xiaolian. She was 28 years old and possessed a beautiful appearance. On the 27th day of the old lunar calendar's tenth month last year, she suddenly disappeared. Xiong Baishu reported the incident to the police and requested an investigation, but more than two months passed without any progress. Until the day before yesterday, Xiong's daughter returned home and recounted the circumstances of her disappearance. She said that on that morning (the 27th of the tenth month), she was lured by Yin Lizhang, a Yangzhou native (Yin and Xiong Baishu were tenants in the same building), to go out and buy cigarettes. As soon as they left the alley entrance, Yin had a car hired in advance, parked nearby. He dragged her into the car, which drove straight to the Huashang Hotel on Haining Road and stopped in front of room number 33. Shortly after, Yin summoned a Yangzhou woman named Cui Tongshi, who stayed with her overnight. The next day, they hired a rickshaw and sent her to Li Moqiu's house at number 3 Qiujiang Road in Zhabei, where she stayed with Li's mother for one night. On the 29th, she was made to marry Li. At first, she was completely unaware, but then she realized what was happening. However, she had no means to resist and had to comply. After cohabitating for two months, she finally seized an opportunity to sneak back, and so on. Xiong Baishu immediately reported this to the Jing'an Temple Police Station, which dispatched a foreign detective and a Chinese detective named Ju Afu to arrest Yin Lizhang and Cui Tongshi. However, Li Moqiu had already gone to Qingdao to do business, so he could not be apprehended. Yesterday morning, the police escorted Yin and the others to the Second Criminal Court of the Special District Local Court. Judge Cheng Shangfeng presided over the hearing. The police's lawyer, Li Zhishan, presented the case. Then, the plaintiff, Xiong Baishu, complained, stating that he had raised Xiaolian from childhood, and she was now sixteen years old. Yin Lizhang had been living with him for about several months, and he explained the previous events. Xiong Xiaolian also testified about the circumstances of her abduction. When questioned, Yin Lizhang confessed that he lived with Xiong. Around September of last year, Xiong's daughter told him that she was being abused by her adoptive father and asked him to find someone for her. He introduced her to Li Moqiu and took her to Li's place, where Xiong's daughter saw him and thought he was suitable. She then married Li. He and Cui Tongshi each received a reward of ten yuan, but Xiong Baishu knew nothing about it, and so on. Cui Tongshi stated that Yin asked her to stay with Xiong's daughter overnight at the Huashang Hotel, and she received ten yuan. She knew nothing else. Judge Cheng announced that the defendants would be detained and a verdict would be delivered next Tuesday. Xiong Xiaolian was allowed to be taken back by Xiong Baishu first.

Lawyers from both sides were present in court. Under questioning by Judge Ying, it appeared that both parties had the possibility of reaching a settlement. Notice from the Cigarette and Exchange Trade Association

▲ Match Transportation and Sales to Other Ports Still Require Registration

▲ Unregistered Cigarettes Cannot Be Sold

The Shanghai Cigarette and Exchange Trade Association stated that for the wholesale transportation and sale of matches to other ports, registration and a certificate are still required in order to be exempt from taxes and released. All unregistered cigarettes must not be wholesaled or sold. Yesterday, the association's Shanghai South Office issued a notice to all members: "We respectfully inform you that on the 21st of this month, the Shanghai Inspection Office of the Su-Zhe-Wan Area Consolidated Tax Bureau issued a letter stating: 'We have received Instruction No. 920 from the Su-Zhe-Wan Area Consolidated Tax Bureau, which states: In accordance with the regulations, the implementation date for the consolidated taxes on cotton yarn, matches, and cement is set for February 1st. It has been found that some goods that were sold by factories before January 31st and are still in stock at various merchants' stores were originally limited to being sold locally and not allowed to be transferred. However, the stocks in various ports inside and outside the city are very abundant. If they were all sold locally, it would be difficult in practice. We have received numerous requests from merchants to allow for a flexible extension for distribution. After considering the situation, our bureau intends to limit these stocks of cotton yarn, matches, and cement to being allowed to be transported by merchants who submit a letter to the bureau before February 28th, listing the brand names and quantities to be transported. Once verified to be correct, a temporary certificate will be issued for transportation, and no further extensions will be granted. Manufacturers outside the area are also allowed to follow the same procedure to ensure fairness. A new form for the temporary certificate has been drafted and submitted to the department for approval. In addition to publishing a notice to inform all merchants with stock, the corresponding inspection office is being notified to comply. If merchants transporting stock have obtained the aforementioned temporary certificate, they should immediately inspect and release the goods in accordance with the regulations and not cause any difficulties. This order is of utmost importance, etc.' A copy of the temporary certificate form is attached to the station. It was previously reported that Dingchang, Yihexinag, Zhentaixiang, Yongfengxiang, Qiuqianfeng, Shenchangxiang, Xiehefeng, Yichengdong, Dongzhaokang, Gonghexing, and Wanchang, had listed their match stock and requested registration. The Su District Bureau had already been petitioned for instructions on the measures to be taken. We now follow the previous instructions. In addition to forwarding the instructions, we are also urgently communicating this information to you for your investigation and immediate notification to all stores. If there are match stocks that you wish to transport and sell to other ports, you must submit a letter to the Su-Zhe-Wan Area Consolidated Tax Bureau (Xianhaiwei Road) before February 28th, listing the brand names and quantities to be transported, for verification and issuance of a temporary certificate for transportation. Please do not miss the deadline and cause yourself problems. This is of utmost importance. The Inspection Office also stated that Yingri Brand, Lanxing Brand, Jiangtaigong Brand, and three types of cigarettes have not been registered and cannot be approved for distribution. Members must not seek small profits and sell them. Once discovered, they will be directly punished. Please inform them by forwarding this notice, etc."

Art World

New Demands on Popular Art by Tang Jun

| Developing towards decorative arts as a foundation for beautifying society |

Because proponents of artistic independence say that the social masses are inherently opposed to unique geniuses, that unique geniuses are fundamentally incomprehensible to the masses, and that art should be isolated from the social masses, standing alone in an "ivory tower," a great misunderstanding arises among the general public regarding the masses and art. They say that art does not belong to the masses, that the masses are fundamentally divorced from art, and upon hearing the phrase "popular art," they exclaim in alarm that pulling art down to the level of the masses would mean the end of art, and that art would perish.

If "popular art" is understood in this way, then what more is there to say? In reality, this is a kind of inherited misunderstanding, and I cannot help but offer some clarification here.

The meaning of "popular art" is not that artists must make their art understandable to the masses, nor that they must pander to the masses. It is not about turning all members of the public into artists. Rather, it means that the public has a certain degree of importance and fondness for art, and that the public has a general capacity for recognition and appreciation of art. In other words, it is about making the appreciation of art "universal" among the masses and making the efficacy and power of art "popular."

Because in certain societies, the appreciation of art is limited to a section of people, or even only a small section, and the efficacy and power of art are only given to a section of people or a small section, there is the promotion of "popular art," in order to enable the majority of the public to have the opportunity to appreciate art, and in order to enable the efficacy and power of art to be given to the majority of the public.

All art inherently possesses "popularity" and "universality." The reason why it sometimes does not become "popular" or "universal" is a matter of improper handling after the art is produced, not a problem with the art itself. It is a matter of art not being applied properly to the masses, not a matter of art not eliciting a response from the masses. The so-called popularization of art is about spreading the soul of art widely into the hearts of the people and scattering the forms of art around the senses of the people, so that their consciousness and senses are subtly influenced by the power of art. Although they cannot create art from innate talent, they can unconditionally and without reason recognize and appreciate art from sensory experience.

Therefore, in order to popularize art, the space of nature should be used as an art gallery to display artworks, and various artworks should be poured out as much as possible among the broad masses. At a certain time, the public's appreciation of art may not achieve a considerable effect, but this is only a matter of time

Page 20

question, not a problem of never being infected. For example, after "Cubism," "Futurism," "Fauvism," "Surrealism," and other artworks were first discovered, most of the general public in Western Europe did not understand them, but now they are treated as everyday occurrences. Even the hats and clothing of ordinary women cannot avoid some Cubist patterns, and new-style lines, either square or round, are often seen on earthen tools. This can all prove that the spirit of modern "plastic arts" (D'art Plastique) is universal among the public in Europe and the West.

However, how can art be popularized, and how can the public be universally artistic? This requires appealing to art with universality! Developing towards practical decorative arts. Why does "practical decorative art" hold such great power over the issue of popularizing art and making the public artistic? Please allow me to explain as follows:

Because practical decorative art is intimately related to the public day and night, and its "beautification" of the public is indefinite. No matter how dull or rough the senses of the public are, after a long period of feeding, they will always be considerably affected.

There are two types of practical decorative art: one is purely practical decorative art, and the other is decorative pure art, such as "decorative painting" (Peinture decorative), "decorative sculpture" (sculpture decorative), and so on.

What people generally mean when they say that we can see artworks as soon as we look up in European and Western countries is that these so-called artworks that can be seen as soon as we look up are all decorated artworks, or can even be called decorative art. From this, we can see the prevalence of decorative art in European and Western countries.

Pure art inherently has popularity. If it is used for decoration, it becomes even more popular, allowing the public to recognize it more intimately. As mentioned above, the reason why Cubism, Futurism, and other arts can exert a considerable influence on the public in Western Europe is because they have undergone a process of "decoration," a process of rendering with a more "popular" decorative meaning. Therefore, the public can receive a kind of infectious power in the face of these decorative arts imperceptibly and lead their senses to develop in the direction of art imperceptibly. If art is only placed in a private small house or a museum, it can only infect a section of people or a small section. It is irrelevant to the majority of the public. Although the public sometimes goes to museums to visit, this is just a sightseeing visit, just a kind of

"A fleeting glance," how much influence does it ultimately have on the interest in art? May I ask how many times can they go to museums for sightseeing, or even have never set foot inside in their lives?

Therefore, the advocacy of popular art should be to popularize art and spread art around the public, so that the general public has the opportunity to come into contact with art every day and immerse their senses in the air of art. This consequently creates the power of popular art, and it also lays a solid foundation for the work of "beautifying society." In order to popularize art, it is necessary to make various forms of art public and present various faces of art to the public. Only by making art "decorative," only by opening up the art hidden in personal small houses as much as possible to the vast exhibition halls of public cities, can this convenience be achieved. Only by vigorously promoting the development of decorative art can this convenience be achieved.
