Youth Forum

Fudan Photography Annual, Being Edited by Tan

The Photography Society of Fudan University in Jiangwan has only been established for three or four years, but the works of its past photography exhibitions have unexpectedly given the audience a very deep and satisfying impression.

Recently, their core members Zhao Yun, Zhang Minguang, Xu Pei, Cao Zuguang, and others have been very busy, often holding meetings. It is said that this is because of the upcoming publication of the "Fudan Photography Annual." The first batch of photos that were printed during their winter vacation have already been proofread, and the final batch is now being printed. It is expected to be published next month. The content includes flowers, still lifes, landscapes, human beauty, etc. The paper used for printing is the highest quality yellow cream-colored woodfree paper, which adds to the beauty. As for the origin of those works, they are very strict, selecting the best from the past member photography exhibitions.

| These few pieces of news are all worth promoting.

Speaking of "Photography Annuals," they have long been very popular and developed in European and American countries. Looking back at the Chinese photography art scene, although there has been a phenomenon of rapid progress in recent years, the call to initiate the publication of a "Chinese Photography Annual" was only heard the year before last, but it has not yet been realized. (Although Lang Jingshan and Du Yu have published individual photography collections.) The difficulty of collecting excellent photos is probably one of the reasons, but the lack of a corresponding understanding of the value of photography art by the society and our group may be one of the biggest reasons.

Now, the "Fudan Photography Annual" is about to be published. In addition to our enthusiastic joy, we sincerely hope that the guardians of the yearbook, the editors, will take good care of it. Then this "annual," which is enough to cause a sensation in the photography art world, may coincide with the satisfactory results we imagined.

Cause and Effect by Yi

The bell for the first class rang. The students obediently walked into the classroom under the loud sound of the bell to seek limitless knowledge. The playground, where there was almost no room to stand, and the grass, which was usually crowded, were now empty, and not even a single solitary figure could be found. Large schools, because they have one thousand five or six hundred students, are usually noisy as anything, but the sound of the class bell can end everything. Apart from the teacher's explanation and the sound of the wind blowing through the trees, no other sounds could be heard.

Mr. Shi, who sat next to Mr. Wang, took advantage of the lecturer's late arrival to show Mr. Wang Miss Kai's "Luanhe Qiude" (according to the transliteration of Love Letter) that was sent to Mr. Li. Because the distance between my seat and Mr. Wang's seat was not too far, I saw a rough outline of the letter's content. In short, it was nothing more than a few trivial and mushy words. My friendship with Mr. Li also has a long history. I will spare myself the announcement of the contents of the letter. The sound of a cockroach-like leather shoe, from far to near, with a foreign "Miss" carrying a handbag stepping into the classroom with the sound of leather shoes, Mr. Wang and Mr. Shi's conversation ended there, and they quietly listened to the teacher lecturing from the textbook.

After class, Mr. Shi said to me like this, "Yesterday afternoon, I bought some things from outside and returned to school. When I passed the gatehouse, I happened to bump into the postman delivering a bunch of letters. I took the opportunity to take a look, and Li's letter was taken from there. Because I and Mr. Li are in the same dormitory, I know a little about the sender of this letter, and I can determine that it is an 'LL'. Last night I was really bored. Mr. Li, who was in the same room, did not come to school, and only I was left in the dormitory. So I opened Li's letter, copied another one, and still sealed it very carefully for him. My methods are really clever. When I handed this letter to Li this morning, he did not detect the flaws in the letter being opened, and he even thanked me 'soundly.'"

In less than two days, Li had another letter. Mr. Shi wanted to try his old trick again, but this time, not only did he not see the slightest hint in the letter, it seemed that he had told Mr. Li that the last letter had also been opened by someone, because just as he was starting, the recipient of this letter suddenly broke in. At this time, Mr. Shi was at a loss and did not know how to answer his friend. At the same time, his face immediately displayed red clouds, as if expressing thirteen points of apology to Li.

The weather has turned cold due to the seasons. Many students are holding hot water bottles and sitting in front of the south-facing auditorium, seeking warmth from a natural large furnace, the sun. A wave of noisy sounds hit my eardrums. Driven by curiosity, I naturally followed the source of the sound. Walking in the corridor of the school, I heard "Who did this prank?", "The lack of morality has reached its extreme."

"·········Love letter·······" A few words.

After hearing these words, I felt as if I was in a fog, unable to distinguish anything. It was not until I reached the room that I knew that Mr. Shi's "letter" had also been opened and read. Poor Mr. Shi, he still doesn't know what's going on. The noise probably occurred because of this letter.

Youth Forum Guidelines

(1) The text should be about discussions on youth issues, domestic and foreign academic or student news, essays, descriptions of school life, casual notes, etc., and the style is not limited.

(2) Books are limited to those related to youth issues.

(3) Photos of youth life (such as sports, travel, sightseeing, drama performances, lectures, gatherings, exhibitions, various competitions, etc.), school news, and youth movements are eligible. Individuals and groups are welcome. (4) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(5) The number of words in each text should not exceed two thousand.

(6) Do not write manuscripts horizontally, do not write carelessly. Western texts can be abbreviated if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not draw pictures with blue ink, and do not use colored paper. Black drawing on white paper is required.

(8) Please specify that the manuscript should be sent to the Editorial Department of the Youth Forum.

(9) Whether or not the submitted manuscript is published, it will not be returned. If a return is required, it should be stated in advance.

(10) Remuneration is divided into three types: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand words. The same applies to books and photos per piece. If there are special manuscripts, the remuneration will be calculated separately.
